SEMINAR WORKS OF THE FINE WORKSHOP.
b

The Art Workshop of the Moscow Proletkult, in its seminar classes on
art history, under the leadership of comrade. Tarabukina, made her first experiments
investigative experiments, using the statistical method in the study of production
denies of easel painting. The object of the study were two authors—Levitsky
and Cezanne.

Methodologically, the work was carried out as follows: based on the basic statistics
stical “law of large numbers”, the largest possible number of pro*
works of this author. The total number of Levitsky's paintings was 50. Cezanne's
all works located in the 1st and 2nd Museums of Western Life were examined
write down Then a series of tasks were outlined, for which all the necessary elements
paintings were subjected to quantitative calculation. Thus, re-
the result was expressed in numerical data, and the conclusion, devoid of any subjective
coloring, achieved maximum objectivity.

To study Levitsky using this method, we took advantage of his exhibition
works arranged by the Tretyakov Gallery. Although not everything is clear at the exhibition,
the paintings were genuine works of this master, but, taking into account,
that the task facing the studio was purely experimental in nature, and also
trying, in order to obtain the most objective data, to attract possible
more extensive quantitative material, the fact was ignored
that some of the paintings in the exhibition are not by Levitsky, but they
yet they are typical exponents of his school. }

The task boiled down to studying the characteristic features of the color of Levits-
whom, for this element is most typical of this’ master. Problem
was divided into three parts: 1) determine the most common colors in the
dozhnik and the size of the area occupied by each color in relation to the area.
the whole canvas, taken as a unit; 2) find out the coloristic rods, on
which holds the main axis of the color composition; 3) set typical
color combinations.

For the first point, the following data was obtained:

The most common color tones are: grayish-pink—41 times, grayish-
white—29 times, gray—30, brown, grayish-brown, grayish-blue
22 times, grayish green—18, red—13, dark gray—12, grayish yellow—12,
golden—11, grayish-black—10. This data was obtained by analyzing each
canvas and fixing each tone in it as a unit, indicating the approximate
no area occupied by it in relation to the entire canvas. The attitude is
taken intenths. Thus, the analysis of all paintings made it possible
establish which tones and in what proportions are most often found in Levitsky,
being, therefore, the most beloved by them. Total count of units of each

Tone made it possible to quantitatively compare all colors with each other, establishing
between them there is a gradation that reveals the artist’s predilection for one or another
color tonality. :

These data lead to the conclusion that in Levitsky’s color scheme
(and his school) there are almost no saturated tones of the spectrum. He operates on the basis of
shady tones, the gradations of shades in which are extremely subtle.

When performing the second task, i.e. when identifying the characteristic color
istic rods on which the axis of the color composition rests, ignored
all the details of color were revealed and only the basic gamut of each
lotna. In this case, it was necessary to establish extreme diversity
the main coloristic ear in the artist’s canvases, But, in contrast
the general nature of Levitsky’s color scheme, based on halftones and complex
nuances of color—the main core of a color composition is often built on the res-
com and expressive comparison of two or more saturated (or approx.
leaning towards saturated) colors. Often these comparisons are juxtaposed
effects of additional colors. For example, a green ribbon cutting a red one
camisole I |

The third task is to establish the most typical color combinations—for now
hall that Levitsky in these combinations proceeded from a consonance of colors, almost not
running to dissonant effects and using extremely diverse techniques
mami. : .

In this third task we came across the need not so much
generalize how much to individualize each canvas. For analysis the most
thin ‘10 authentic and undeniable paintings by the master were identified. Lead
the results of the analysis of each canvas would be difficult here, due to
limited space.

In connection with this last problem, otherother elements
Levitsky's painting: texture, pictorial form does not have such a connection
< color, due to which one could talk about the close dependence of these two
elements. The pictorial form itself has two characters: wit and
softness. An example. The first is the oval portrait of Mniszech, and the example of the second is
portrait of Lion. A closer connection can be found between the visual arts
shape and texture. The surface of the first portrait and others like it is painted
extremely carefully. .

All traces of the work process are hidden in the tightly compressed texture. On-.
against, in portraits, an example of a pictorial manner of writing of which is
portrait of Lvova, the softness of the pictorial form is equally expressively emphasized
chickpeas and in a soft brushstroke manner, leaving the process of working on it unhidden
texture. Both of these manners were inherent in Levitsky at the same time, and chronologically
It is impossible to physically determine their shift. Although Levitsky used Lesirovnaya, he

The compositional side of Levitsky’s portraits is not significant
interest. In most cases, it is built on a central vertical

writing, we have to say with certainty that in his best works (on
this exhibition is far from numerous) Levitsky achieved exceptional
strength and compactness. in processing material mass and high perfection
skill in craftsmanship. }

I.

The work on Cezanne’s canvases differed significantly in method from similar
noi’ work on Levitsky’s works.

As the analysis of Cezanne's paintings deepened, it was necessary not to
generalize as much as individualize in an extremely diverse manner
this master, who was constantly in search of the highest perfection
stva. Some paintings were isolated and analyzed in detail. In view of
specialties of such analysis, individual examples will not be given, but indicated
there will be only general conclusions. Research work onand Cezanne's painting
made it even more complicated. that a number of elements of a painting, without playing
which have a significant role in Levitsky (for example, composition), they acquire from Cezanne
special meaning.

In Cezanne, the main path of his creative aspirations is easily revealed,
to whom all the resources of his mastery are subordinated. The basis of his painting is
compositional resolution of the pictorial form of the visually perceived
subject. A collision between a three-dimensional object and a two-dimensional plane, on
in which this three-dimensional object should be picturesquely constructed, Cezanne designed
solves through color and perspective illusion. “Thus, for the sake of
illusionistic interpretation of the three-dimensional shape of an object on a canvas, Cezanne
transforms elements such as color, composition,
texture, etc., which other contemporary painters had quite the same
modulating meaning.

In Cezanne, two styles of writing can be distinguished: the most impressionistic
cultural, found mainly in landscapes that, apparently, were in
in most cases, only sketches made “on motives” (as he put it),
and the second manner, constructive, - for Cezanne more typical and common
mainly in still lifes and finished pieces he made in his own
workshop and carefully crafted.

A number of works in which part of the canvas was left behind for unknown reasons
finished (for example, still lifes in the former Morozov Gallery), are opened
the artist's creative process. From it it can be established that although Cezanne worked
botal “thinking with a brush in his hands,” nevertheless, he strived as a result of his
work to hide its rough, procedural side.

His well-known formula for constructing the shape of an object based on a ball,
cube and cone were for him only “scaffolding” when constructing a picturesque building,
“scaffoldings” that were removed when the work was finished. On the mentioned still-
Mortakh this is noticeable with complete clarity. So, on the right side of both still lifes
products in the figurative form of folds of napkins and in fruktahs are easy to spot
elements of geometric forms, but they disappear in the left complete part of these
same paintings.

Trying to express the three-dimensionality of the shape of an object with the greatest specificity,
In reality, Cezanne sometimes resorted to unfolding an object on a plane, although
and not to the same extent as his Cubist followers. To do this, he sometimes changed
“point of view” several times, thereby changing the perspective. In some
He has two or three points of view on things. Indicative of this
№9 PROLECULES 115

th

sense, one of the still lifes in the former Morozov gallery, in which the table and
some of the objects are deployed from one position, the jug standing closer to the left
parts of the canvas, reveals a different point of view, and the floor and part of the steva,
undoubtedly taken again from a new position.

Observations on surface treatment in the field are extremely instructive.
Cezanne's lots. He prescribed them with great care and tenacity,
covering the same place several times in succession with different tones
flowers. His palette was varied; the stroke is dense, short and thin
in the sense of a paint layer. Over one square centimeter he has
It is difficult to find two completely homogeneous color strokes. It's rich-
he achieved a variety of nuances quite often by mixing colors
canvas. :

In Cezanne, composition is often subordinated to the same tasks of illusory
to clearly identify the shape of depicted objects. Constructive design
material mass of the canvas, in its own way. amazing craftsmanship, opens up the artistic
Nick has a lot of instructive stuff. .

Despite the fact that these seminars were conducted in the area of problems
easel painting, students of the Iso workshop recognize their fruitfulness and for
their production work for which their workshop prepares them. Like Levitsky,
like Cezanne, they found an example of highly skilled craftsmanship over
material and in many cases the most perfect resolution is purely professional
national tasks of painting. Their methods can be translated into Englishnew language
production work of modern art craftsmanship.

In addition, for future purely instructor activities, which will have to
graduates of the workshop will encounter the experience and method of seminar work not only
did not pass without a trace, but brought its undoubted results, which will
taken into account in practical work.

IVANOVO-VOZNESENSKY PROLETNULT.

The Ivanovo-Voznesensky Proletkult has a strong theater collection.
Tiv, very prepared in terms of craftsmanship.

holiday, participating, among other things, in the carnival organized on this day.
